@ehsanmasdar
10/14/2014 11:24

We have noticed that the kickstand can become locked into the cutout in the base and will not Release by driving into it. In fact, in several cases the robot has spun around facing the center goal assembly and drove up the kickstand and flipped over. On page 13 of the Field Assembly and Setup Guide, it states (including typo) in step 4 that, Kickstands are positioned to hold up ball tray with the bottom of the pipe sitting (type, missing language) the base cutouts. When the kickstand is centered in the base cutout it is difficult and sometimes impossible to dislodge even in Teleop mode. It seems to me that the intent of this game element especially during Autonomous mode is to be able to navigate to the kickstand and bump it out of the base and not to have to lift the kickstand out of the base once there. Could the setup instructions allow for the kickstand to be positioned on the outer edge of the base cutout or include a plate under the base to keep the kickstand from sinking into the foam floor. This, or a similar modification/clarification, would allow for a consistent Release of the kickstand across venues, during Autonomous mode and quicker release during Teleop.

Answer: There will be no modification of the setup for the Kickstand. The lower end of the Kickstand should be placed within the circular cutout in the Center Field Structure baseplate.

Ehsan Asdar

@ehsanmasdar
10/14/2014 12:25
Quote:




            Originally Posted by FTC5559


        I've notice our the bearing ball casters on the rolling goal are starting to get rusty, making it difficult to roll the goals around.

Will new bearing ball casters be used for each event?

Please see the following recommendation from AndyMark for ball casters that become rusty, as ball caters will not be replaced from event to event:

  1. Remove the plastic cap holding in the steel ball by using a flat head screwdriver. Place the screwdriver in the seam between the cap and the plastic base.
  2. Pry the cap away from the base until it comes loose and is removed from the base.
  3. Remove the steel ball from the socket.
  4. Put a small bit of light oil, such as mineral oil, on a rag.
  5. Wipe the oily rag over the steel ball, applying pressure to the rusty area.
  6. Rust or marks from rust may not be totally removed, but the ball should be smooth when finished.
  7. Use a second rag, one that is dry, to wipe the oil from the ball
  8. Place ball back into the socket
  9. Reattach plastic cap

Ehsan Asdar

Ehsan Asdar

@ehsanmasdar
10/19/2014 16:26
Quote:




            Originally Posted by FTC5559


        I've notice our the bearing ball casters on the rolling goal are starting to get rusty, making it difficult to roll the goals around.

Will new bearing ball casters be used for each event?

Please see the following recommendation from AndyMark for ball casters that become rusty, as ball caters will not be replaced from event to event:

  1. Remove the plastic cap holding in the steel ball by using a flat head screwdriver. Place the screwdriver in the seam between the cap and the plastic base.
  2. Pry the cap away from the base until it comes loose and is removed from the base.
  3. Remove the steel ball from the socket.
  4. Put a small bit of light oil, such as mineral oil, on a rag.
  5. Wipe the oily rag over the steel ball, applying pressure to the rusty area.
  6. Rust or marks from rust may not be totally removed, but the ball should be smooth when finished.
  7. Use a second rag, one that is dry, to wipe the oil from the ball
  8. Place ball back into the socket
  9. Reattach plastic cap

@ehsanmasdar
11/5/2014 19:46

GS8 prohibits deliberate contact with a Ball Tube and assesses a Minor Penalty for grabbing the Ball Tube of a Rolling Goal. GS8 does not mention the Center Goal explicitly.

The definitions are unclear whether a Center Goal has a Ball Tube. A Ball Tube is the scoring part of a Goal, of which there are two types: Rolling Goal and Center Goal. The definition of a Rolling Goal mentions a Ball Tube, but the definition of a Center Goal does not explicitly mention a Ball Tube. However, Section 1.4.4 says that scoring is the Center Goal is based on Ball Height, and Ball Height is an attribute of a Ball Tube.

Could you please clarify: Is the score part of the Center Goal considered a Ball Tube? More relevant: Is grabbing or deliberate contact with the Center Goal allowed?

**Answer: The tube that is part of the Center Goal is a Ball Tube. The Center Goal has the same rules applied to is as the Rolling Goals; i.e.:

GS5 Descoring GS8 GS9 Non-incidental contact with the Ball Tube GS14 Tipping

Penalties associated with the above rules will all apply to inappropriate interaction with the Center Goal Ball Tube**

@ehsanmasdar
2/18/2015 10:34
Quote:




            Originally Posted by FTC5873


        In the Game Manual Part I, section 8.2 FTC Award Eligibility says in part,

… To ensure fairness to all teams and to provide equal opportunity for all teams to win an award at an FTC Championship tournament, teams are only eligible to win an award at the first three Championship tournaments that they attend. Those teams who compete in more than three Qualifying Tournament, League Championships, and Championship tournaments do so for the purpose of being involved in the fun and excitement of the tournament and not with the intention of winning awards or advancing to the next tournament level. … Is it correct to say that teams that have participated in three Qualifying Tournaments are ineligible to receive any judged award at subsequent Qualifying Tournaments?

Is it correct to say that a team which is participating in its fourth Qualifying Tournament will not earn advancement to that Region’s Championship from this fourth Qualifying Tournament, regardless of their team’s on-field performance or recognition by the judges?

Does either answer change if the Qualifying Tournaments are in different Regions?

Thanks for the great questions!

The limits apply at every level and are based on the event the team would advance to. A team could conceivably compete at 3 Qualifying Tournaments in New Jersey and still be eligible for advancement or award consideration at a Qualifying Tournament in Pennsylvania. Further, a team could win the Inspire Award at Qualifying Tournament or League Championship in New Jersey, and still be eligible for consideration of that award at a League Championship or Qualifying Tournament in Pennsylvania.

At a State or Regional Championship level, the same guidelines apply. A team could be eligible for awards and/or advancement at 3 State or Regional Championships within an area covered by the East Super-Regional, and would remain eligible for awards and/or advancement at a State or Regional Championship within an area covered by the North, South or West Super-Regional. A team who has already secured a spot at a Super Regional must declare which Super Regional they plan to attend - a team may not advance to multiple Super Regional events.

FTC Robot Driver Certification

Update 9/16/2014 from Danny

USB hubs, in general, are all absolute crap. It turns out that manufacturers absolutely believe that if you put 4 ports on a device, only half of the ports will be actually transmitting data at any given time. Therefore, with 99% of the USB hubs out there, if you plug 4 devices on a 4-port hub and actually use them all at the same time, data will stop transmitting on some of the devices randomly because the hardware can’t handle the switching. Yes, I said switching - it’s not a bandwidth problem, it’s a switching problem (they cheaped out on components which maintains signal integrity while switching inputs). That spans all of the major manufacturers, and all of the minor ones too. It’s recommended that if you’re actually going to use 4 ports simultaneously, you need a 7-port or bigger hub - they have bigger/beefier/better switches in them. Anker consistently produces the best hubs in the business (but they only make USB 3.0 hubs and are 2-3x more expensive - you don’t NEED USB 3.0, but most everything being made is USB 3.0 today) - RocketFish USB hubs was our top choice hub, but they are no longer being made. You might want to talk to Rad Allen to see what he recommends as a replacement to the RocketFish (if he’s tested for a replacement), he burned through lots of hubs before he found the RocketFish. But, if you want something bullet-proof, buy two 7-port Anker USB 3.0 hubs and you’ll hurt a little in the pocketbook but you’ll be happier in the long run.

AND, your hubs are required to have external power. None of this “USB powered hub” crap, you actually need an outside power source. 4 joysticks pull too much power, it might work a while but eventually it will look like the USB port on the computer “fails” because too much power is being pulled. If you have an externally-powered hub, the joysticks plugged into the hub get their power from the external power and not the power from the computer. Beware of “cheap” externally-powered units, the RocketFish hubs that we love so much have incredibly crappy external power plugs, and some of them will cause interference when plugged in!

Cable lengths are important to note as well. USB 2.0 has a max cable length of about 16 feet (5 meters), but you should never really use a cable over 10 feet long (3 meters) - after 10 feet the signal starts to become “iffy” and after 14 feet the signal is “unreliable.” USB 3.0 recommends nothing longer than 9 feet (3 meters) ever. Now, you can get USB cables that can extend beyond 16’ - “Active Extension” or “Repeater” cables will boost the signal and transmit or “repeat” the signal halfway down the cable length (depending on the cable type). These have been known to work, but nobody’s really done a thorough testing of these for use in FTC.

So, the answers are:

a. Use active extension cables when going beyond 3 meters (9 feet). Some active cables extend to 32’, and some can be chained (allowing you to have multiple 16’ segments). b. Buy Anker USB 3.0 7-port hubs. c. See (a). d. See (b).

Actual questions to Danny: (a) Can USB 2 handle the 20 foot cable length for this application?

(b) Should we buy all USB 3 - hubs and cables (the laptop has a USB 3) - or will USB 2 handle it ok?

(c) Should we try to “balance” the wire length and have the 2-port hub somewhere at the half way point (near the power outlet in the drawing), and then have RED and YELLOW wires of about 12 feet each? BLUE would then be around 12-15 feet.

(d) Are there recommended hubs or are they pretty much equal?

Driver practice is critical to our success. We would like to give as many of the team that is interested in driving, the chance to drive. However, there is a process and controls. Absolutely no driving FTC robots without certification. If you don’t know that you are certified, you are not certified. See Gerry first if you aren’t sure how to proceed.

The 4290 “Block Party” robot cost about $2000 to build. We want to limit the damage to the robots from un-trained driving. Drivers must be trained and checked out by a someone from the set of team members who understand the controls and can help train the new folks. The “control button configuration” for each robot will be posted on the wall in the shop by the FTC field.

Once certified in robot operation and Field Control System (FCS) setup, students can set-up (and clean up when they are done) FTC robots that they are certified for during field “free time”. Failure to cleanup and put away the robots and field equipment when you are done practicing will be cause for you to loose your certification to drive.

We will be establishing a schedule so there are “slots” that people can come in and reasonably expect the field to be used for practice. The other legitimate use is “autonomous” testing by the software team. The field is a shared resource and has to be treated as such. Often, both autonomous testing and tele-op could be going on at the same time. Sometimes, we may have to give priority to the hardware team, software team or drive team for specific testing. We’ll consider the best use of the field at that time as a team.

@arthurpachachura1 The firmware does not really matter since the devices are both running Android on top. From my understanding we are going to be able to use pure vanilla Android Studio with Gradle/ART, but probably some sort of FTC library included for delegating tasks to sensors and motors via their power brick. The exciting thing (if it turns out this way) is that it seems we will be designing two apps - one for the robot and one for the driver station … which means that we could write a full fledged touch enabled gui using the Android framework for things like the options api and have the drivers simply select the options they want on the screen!

Tetrix Battery charging

For future reference, I’m not sure if Tetrix batteries like being left to charge overnight: once charged, they get hot, fast. We should find out whether it’s okay to do so.

Daniel Teal

9/9/2014 19:03

Izzy brought up a good point: this can be a library of part modules for anything (rather than only manipulators). We can build, say, a mecum module with a wheel and motor that has standard Tetrix mounting holes. It’d be made of glued laser cut plywood and could be fastened to other parts with either #6 or 5/16” bolts.

This would be a nice solution to the massive design problem we face trying to make this year’s robot’s complexity solely with panels. Plus, we should be able to replace individual modules.

Schedule Coordination software

This probably exists…so no one just go off and write it!!!!

The idea is we need a way to schedule time in the shop or on Robotics activities. If would be nice to know some of the following things:

  • Arthur will be out every Wednesday
  • Ehsan leaves early on Tuesday
  • Daniel will not be here today (last minute emergency), can be reached via phone and is interruptable.

It would be nice to have an easy way to toggle your intent from a “standard” schedule you keep. So by default, you are in certain days, and out others. If you “toggle” it, it will say you are doing the opposite today. I normally would be there, but I have a test today. I can’t be there, so I’ll mark myself as NOT coming in. Something like that. Instead of toggle, you just may have a simple (here or not here) sent via text or a custom app.

As I said, we need to do some research first and see if it exists. If not, then maybe we build something simple?

FLL Coaches Kickoff - Sep 27

Coaches’ Kick-Off is designed to get your team ready for this year’s challenge. The event includes a program and season overview, resources for coaches and mentors grant opportunities, mentor recruitment sources, a walk-thru of the challenge field and much more!

Coaches’ Kick-Off is recommended for ADULTS currently involved in FIRST® Tech Challenge as well as adults interested in learning more about becoming a coach, mentor, judge or referee. Two team members (students) per team maximum. Refreshments will be provided.

Dot Bot - FLL Skills volunteer(s) - needed ASAP

#Background

The Dot Bots are a rookie FLL team formed at the Texas School for the Blind and Visually Impaired (TSBVI). LASA Robotics mentors this team and in particular, Gerry is the co-Coach of this team. Two years ago, Gerry and the co-Coach from TSBVI (Dr Kay Pruett) formed one of the first Blind teams competing in FLL. The “original” Dot Bots won as co-champions at their qualifier at Connally HS in Austin against 23 other sighted teams. They went on to finish 31st out of 60 teams in robot performance at their Regional Qualifer, and sadly did no move forward. Last year, we did not have enough interested members to field a team. This year we have 4 blind students and 2 visually impaired students on the team and excited to compete.

#Help Needed

We need some help from our LASA students. What we need in the short term is this:

Super FLL Builder Skills - As FLL coach, I cannot design or build the robot. I can help select a design (from online or another source) and guide the kids in building that robot. Since every member of the blind team runs the robot at the table in competition (it’s just something we do), we have some specific requirements that must be incorporated into a design. This turns out to be hard to find.

If you are interested in helping on this “outreach” activity (you will get outreach hours for this - which counts toward travel requirements), let me know and lets talk. PHreshman with “fresh” FLL skills are of considerable interest to me :-).

Requirments for Base robot:

a) Easy access to battery compartment
b) Easy access to NXT Controls
c) Easy access to Charger Port
d) Medium size fat, flat tires
e) Roller ball for slider (from EV3 kit)
f) Alignment
    i) Flat back for Bump Turns
    ii) Alignment with tri-direction corner "jig"
g) thoughtful placement for attachment motor
i) NO attachments should be made (team does those)

FLL Game model builder(s) - This years game is released, but we don’t have the kit yet. When it comes in, we will need help putting all the gave pieces together. I plan on bringing it to LASA one afternoon and get help from the team. Someone needs to take point on this task.

The above work can be done at LASA and I’ll shuttle the parts and pieces back and forth.

We may need some more one-on-one building help at TSBVI in the future. If you are interested, leave a comment below so I know that. You can always say no later, but it would be nice to know who to go to and ask for help!

Some more background info - 9/14/2014 Here are the pictures of the bots we used in the Senior Solutions Challenge. The second one is closer to what I’m looking for (PHighter Too).

Notice the “two way” jig for leaving the base to the north or east. This year, the jig needs to allow leaving north, east and north-east!

Freescale 1/18 scale car - Oct 17

Freescale’s Tiny Town Drive-In Theatre Car Contest Requirements: • Scale of the Drive In is ~1:18-1:14, so we want vehicles to be roughly in that range of size • Vehicles must be robust and weatherproof, able to stay outdoors for several weeks without damage (Rain, freezing, UV exposure, etc) • Wheels do not need to operate (cars won’t be moved) • Moving parts are not recommended due to likelihood of mechanical failures in the field • Cars will be viewed from a distance of ~15-20 feet away, so small details will likely not be visible

  1. DIMENSIONS: Standard cars should be ~6” high x ~6” wide x ~14” long (sedan type car) - in keeping with ~1:18-1:16 scale. Larger vehicles just need to be in scale.
  2. MATERIALS: Can be wood, metal, or plastic. Wood and metal preferred, but all must be fully painted (including plastics) to protect from the elements; Windshields can be clear plastic, tempered glass, or simply open. Glass should be tempered glass for safety and plastic will likely cloud after exposure to UV, so some provision for replacement or removal should be allowed.
  3. MOUNTING: o Must have painted wood block under center of car, painted flat black with a footprint of 3” x 5” o This block must be securely attached to car o All cars will be screwed down to the parking area using this block as an anchor (theft prevention & ease of setup)
  4. LIGHTING: o LED tail lights, parking lights, or interior lights are welcomed addition (no headlights or bright brakelights, please) o Cars will have access to 12V DC power, no more than ~100mA per car. o Any lighting must have a brightness control adjustment to control intensity (so we can balance relative brightness of cars) - namely a potentiometer
  5. BONUS POINTS (extra consideration) will be given for extra creativity!
    Some ideas: o Themed cars (school colors/mascot for local schools) o Electroluminescent Lighting (EL) lighting effects for neon o Miniature art cars o Convertibles with people inside o Lego car o Movie themed car(s) (Batmobile, Back-to-the-Future DeLorean, Lightning McQueen, A-team van, Herbie, Mystery Machine, etc.) o Sleigh with Reindeer…

FTC - Vandegrift Open - Nov 15

EDIT: 10/14/2014

I want to send out the details for our 3rd Annual ViperBot Open on 11/15. Last year we had 22 teams participate. I will be capping this year’s event at 30 teams. Please share with other coaches in the area that you have contact with. SkillPoint is supposed to include this in their next 10/20 email blast, but wanted to give you all a heads up.

3rd Annual ViperBot Open Saturday, 11/15 8:00 am – 2:00 pm Doors open at 7:00 am Format: Qualification Rounds, Elimination Rounds, Awards Cost is Free

Special Awards for Best Autonomous, Most Balls Scored, High Score, Quickest Score, Most End Game Points

Registration: Send team names, team numbers, and team contact info to Rad Allen at irad.allen@leanderisd.org

The ViperBot Open (scrimmage) is a fairly informal event. We will give you a table to set up for your area, but no one sets us a formal pit with marketing, decorations, etc.

There is no judging at this event. It is purely an “on-field” competition run in the same fashion as the performance part of the FTC competitions.

Each team will compete in at least 5 rounds. We rank the teams, choose alliance partners, then conduct elimination rounds. Last year we had 18 teams.

We have trophies for Winning Alliance and Finalist Alliance. We also give special awards based on this year’s game. For example, last year we gave trophies for :

  • Alliance with the highest score (last year is was 219)
    • Alliance with the most blocks scored in teleop (last year was 32 blocks)
  • Team with best autonomous - most points scored in autonomous during qualification rounds
  • Team that scored the fastest block in teleop (last year was 8 seconds)

We will determine this year’s special awards after the game is released.

Although last year there were no formal inspections (either hw or sw), this year we will be training inspectors. So, there will be some sort of inspection process.

We are entertaining the idea of running “mock judging” rounds to give teams some feedback.

As we get closer to the event, we will have more details.

Hope this helps.

Rad Allen

=================== ​ From Rick Morales, Freescale:

First and foremost, THANK YOU for your enthusiasm for the various events. In total there will be 20+ teams and well over 150 coaches, mentors and students involved in some way over the weekend. For that we are very appreciative. We see this as an opportunity to showcase robotics and the future innovators that you are coach. Key thing is for you and the team to have fun!

NEW While at the Marathon Runners Expo, make sure to walk your team through the Freescale Internet of Things Truck which will be located caddy corner to where the robot demos will be. You will be able to see Freescale-enabled IoT devices in operation today and understand how they will evolve across multiple technology areas like home, medical, cities and more.

The three-story truck contains 120+ demos from the smallest micros to complex network infrastructure. You can test drive data aggregators, ADAS, wearables, telepresence robots and myoelectric gesture recognition technology. Freescale and our partners also use this vehicle to train, design solutions and explore interactive webinars and presentations.

IR Beacon

The IR Beacon is finicky. We need to know it inside and out.

excerpt from attached paper:

  • Beginning in the 2013-2014 season Hitechnic introduced 360 degree IR beacon (#HBK2100). This beacon replaces the previous, 180 degree IR beacon (#FTCBCN). Both types of beacons are allowed at events during the 2013-2014 season. However, team’s should note that due to differences in the placement of the IR LEDs, the measured output from the new style beacon will be different (typically lower in magnitude) than the measured output from the old style beacon.

From field build instructions, we will not have a field with “mixed” type of IR sensors, but we can expect EITHER type. We will have to be sure we know what type is in use and be able to switch between them.

Gerry Cocco

Mecanum Autonomous

This is where the rubber hits the road. Can we move the robot exactly where we want to in a repeatable, autonomous fashion. Hopefully all the gyro work will pay off on this item.

Checklist

work on basic movement routines - with gyro feedback.
Basic straight line
Basic turns (45 degree, 90 degree)
Random angle turn (eg 33 degree, left or right)
distance challenge - based on TIME
distance challenges - based on ROTATIONs
success: able to go straight, 90 left or right, 45 degree - left or right
save out this work as a major release Mecanum
code review and sign off from Gerry

Marek Travnikar - Mentor

@marektravnikar
8/16/2014 20:48

An idea I wanted to throw in (I think this is the best spot) is omni wheels on encoders. I have implemented a quick and crude system on two omni wheels on the Octanum bot and (when combined with gyro data) was VERY pleased with how well it could track position of the robot (down to 1/8” even after wild and crazy driving). These wheels only can work on flat portions of the field (if must touch the ground to work) but that could still be very useful for a challenge such as last years, where setting up and running the autonomous would be a breeze and very robust. Essentially this improves on the “straight line move” from moving and staying pointed in a direction, to correcting any drift in may have in the process. I know we are going to use this system for FRC and HRR and most probably FRC next year (unless we find an even better method) because it is so easy and effective. Just food for thought.

Arthur Pachachura

@arthurpachachura1
8/17/2014 07:35

That sounds great, but I think FTC (non-freshman team) is committed to Mecanum 4WD. If you think the same works with Mecanum wheels, it could be worth a shot.

Marek Travnikar - Mentor

@marektravnikar
8/17/2014 19:42

Oh, sorry, I must have not explained it well. In addition to the mecanum wheels you have two small unpowered omni wheels near the center of the robot that are attached to encoders. That way there is no risk of a slip in the wheel, and are able to tell any kind of movement, intended or not (see FRC trello for a picture on the FRC octanum).

Ehsan Asdar

@ehsanmasdar
6/6/2014 10:54

http://www.patronumbots.com/uploads/1/3/1/6/13161577/hitechnic_motor_controller_-_brief_v1.3.pdf Resources for i2c communication for hitechnic motor controller. Seems that daisy chain assigns address 0x02 to the controller attached to nxt, then 0x04, 0x06 ect. So we can loop through all the addresses we expect (depending on how many we daisy chain) and look for something like bit 10 – 17H(sensorname) or 00 – 07H (sensor version) to id the sensor as a motor controller. After this, we can also read the D6 bit to make sure that the motor controller does not have an “ERROR” (it shuts down and sets this if it detects a short circuit, overcurrent, or other issue)

Marek Travnikar - Mentor

@marektravnikar
12/7/2014 16:23

Ok we need a clarification on post #52. It indeed now says LED’s can be used for the purpose of communicating with team members, however it states that for LED’s that are controlled by the NXT (i.e. non decorative). They must be “controlled and powered only by connections to a HiTechnic SuperPro Prototype Board.” However, if there were to be true, even with the optional 9V battery added, we would be limited to an incredible 2 LEDs, since each LED uses 20mA. This does not sound right at all. If we were to use something like an LED strip, we could signal it off of a arduino on the prototype board (that signal using micro amps) and then power it off of the main battery (as is done with decorative lighting). We should clarify this, since as it stands, decorative lighting is effectively limited to 2 small, hard to see, 5mm LEDs.

Ehsan Asdar

@ehsanmasdar

Daniel Teal

@dteal
12/7/2014 20:20

I posted this question:

“Our team would like to use LED lights in a similar manner to Team 0025’s description in post #52, i.e., as sensor feedback and an end game warning to drivers during teleop and purely as decoration before and after teleop. According to , such LEDs must be controlled and powered only by connections to a HiTechnic SuperPro Prototype Board or the NXT Prototype Board.

However, post #4 states and post #11 confirms that all used power in this case must come from the prototype board, which, with a 9v battery, has a limit of 8mA at 9V, 50 mA at 5V, and 20 mA at 3.3V. But when a single LED draws 20 mA, there’s no way we can power, say, an RGB light strip (http://www.adafruit.com/product/306 : Digital RGB LED Weatherproof Strip - LPD8806 32 LED - (1m) : 120 mA per 2.5”), not to mention a microcontroller to drive it.

Is there any legal way that we can make the NXT control an LED light strip?

Thank you.”

Hopefully that will get us somewhere. If not, perhaps we can try a self-contained (but programmable) LED strip like “BlikyTape”: http://www.adafruit.com/product/1605. That would give us some neat patterns, but the lights couldn’t correspond to anything that the NXT does.

Ehsan Asdar

@ehsanmasdar
12/7/2014 20:24

@danielteal1 I think the idea was that R 11.e 1 states that we can use the main robot battery, but post #52 says power must come from the prototype board. The question, in my mind at least, is not “is there any legal way” but is more “can we power non decorative leds off the main robot battery”

Daniel Teal

@dteal
12/7/2014 20:28

@ehsanmasdar That makes sense. The rule does say “LEDs controlled by the Robot must be controlled and powered only by connections to a HiTechnic SuperPro Prototype Board or the NXT Prototype Board.” I’m curious as to what they’ll answer to our post; perhaps they will suggest using the main battery somehow.

Marek Travnikar - Mentor

@marektravnikar
12/9/2014 20:59

@ehsanmasdar @danielteal1 @gerrycocco “A: As you noted, any circuit connected to the prototype board (including microcontrollers and any attached LEDs) must not exceed the board’s power limits that you included (from the post dated 09-22-2014, 12:46 PM). In order to control an LED light strip you would have to find one that can be operated within these limits, including all associated control circuits.”

We might have a problem doing this the easy way… But what if there was another way?

Clearly we can not electrically connect a LED light strip to the NXT in any way, but what if we didn’t do it electrically? By R11.e.i we can connect LED strips to the battery, and presumably this means the controller (Arduino) to control them too, right? What if we had, say, a servo that turned a potentiometer that connected to the controller? Does anyone see any legality issues with this? Clearly their intent is to separate the robot battery from the NXT by all means, and this does exactly that. In fact, in the end, it very well might be an easier interface than trying to get I2C working on both sides. Thoughts?

EDIT: AND it doesn’t need a MUX.

Marek Travnikar - Mentor

@marektravnikar
12/9/2014 21:12

@danielteal1 @ehsanmasdar @gerrycocco The closest I can see to this violating a rule is “ LEDs controlled by the Robot must be controlled and powered only by connections to a HiTechnic SuperPro Prototype Board or the NXT Prototype Board.”

However, I feel like this would be a violation in letter but not spirit. We may want to ask for a clarification on the ambiguous use of “controlled” and “connections,” or we might be able to justify it as is.

Gerry Cocco

@gerrycocco
12/9/2014 21:48

The following came over the transom into our email….

———- Forwarded message ———- From: Craig MacFarlane camacfarl@gmail.com Date: Tue, Dec 9, 2014 at 5:21 PM Subject: Controlling LEDs from the protoboard. To: lasa418@gmail.com, Team team@rocknrollrobots25.com

Team Lasa,

I noticed you referenced Team 25 in a FTC Forum post.

http://ftcforum.usfirst.org/showthread.php?3034-Robot-Electronics-and-Power-Answer-Thread&p=11814&viewfull=1#post11814

I wrote up a blog post on what I did last year that has pictures and a description of what was done.

http://degreesplato.wordpress.com/2014/02/04/robots-need-lights/

It essentially boils down to having to use a bare bones atmel microcontroller burned with an Arduino bootloader. Most teams’ first instinct is to use an Arduino, but all that circuitry on the board around the microcontroller consumes way too much current.

Note that if you do this, you want the ATMega328p, the ‘p’ standing for pico power.

Craig

Electronics Standards - Style guide

  • what should our defaults be in connecting motors and sensors
  • sticking with standard configurations, will make software less error prone
  • having a known, workable connection “style” will make maintenance easier
  • CAD work can take this into account also

SO FAR:

Without:

Port 1: Motor controllers (4 daisy, power shared) Port 2: Servo controllers (2 daisy, power shared) Port 3: IR Sensor/Prototype Board Port 4: Gyro Sensor/Limit Switch/IR Sensor (IR Sensor is an option IFF Prototype on port 3) With:

Port 1: Motor controllers (4 daisy, power shared) Port 2: Servo controllers (2 daisy, power shared) Port 3: Prototype Board (Write action not supported by mux so it gets its own port) Port 4: Mux Mux 1: IR Sensor Mux 2: Gyro Sensor Mux 3: Limit Switch / Other Mux 4: Limit Switch / Other

Checklist

Is there a delay if motors are not on same motor controller?

Ehsan Asdar

@ehsanmasdar
8/31/2014 16:57

Ok after doing a bit of research, here is the best I could come up with. NXT port 1- 4 daisy chained motor controllers (which is the maximum) and also gives us 8 motor ports (the maximum allowed). First motor controller is the front two drive motors, second motor controller is the back two driver motors. Motor controller 3/4 for any extra needed for manipulation, and obviously if we dont need controller 4 we wont include it!

NXT Port 2- Two daisy chained servo controllers giving us the ability to control the max (12) servos. If we dont need servo controller two, again, we dont have to include it.

NXT Port 3/4: Other sensors. This could include limit switches to prevent robot breaking, and IR sensor, a gyro sensor, a prototype board, or anything else we could conceivably use. Since we plan on using a gyro this year and the challenge will most likely include IR, I would caution that we should build the robot to design around the possibility that we will have no space for limit switches. Thoughts @gerrycocco?

Gerry Cocco

@gerrycocco
8/31/2014 17:05

What about the Prototype board?

Daniel Teal

@dteal
7/24/2014 12:33

I’ve successfully 3D printed Tetrix-like gears in black ABS plastic. They are nearly as strong with comparable negligible backlash. Plus, they weigh about 18% of the original aluminum gears, and assuming $40 per kilo of ABS and Lego Education prices, cost 40¢ altogether or about 98.6% less!

Daniel Teal

@dteal
7/24/2014 12:36

My thought is to integrate these with the mecanum wheel mounting hubs for extra strength. We can use them in other parts of the robot, too, of course. For competition I’ll probably make them a bit thicker and in herringbone style: http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herringbone_gear.

Gerry Cocco

@gerrycocco
7/24/2014 13:44

I like the printed gears. Cheaper and you can make whatever size you need (within reason :-). The herringbone patter gears also look promising. Keep us posted.

Daniel Teal

@dteal
8/2/2014 17:08

(1) Marek’s prototype beam made of lasercut .25” plywood is amazing; that should easily be strong enough for the robot.

(2) The lasercut gears are good, but don’t seem to have any advantage over the printed ones.

Mecanum Field Oriented Drive

Take the Q&D mecanum mule and add a gyro. Modify the Mecanum.1 code (with no frills and bells) to drive in a Field Oriented Drive (FOD) mode. This code should be bare bones, since it will be used as reference for later work.

Checklist

Add only one operator control to allow robot to be turned on its Z-axis.
tele-op moves in FOD fashion, rock solid
ensure event control loop is fully responsive (no thread hogs)
get some driver feedback
code review and sign off from Gerry
save out this as minor release Mecanum-3

Suggested reading for D5 (design)

#Background D5 (Drop Dead Design Day Do-over) is the somewhat tongue-in-cheek acronym for our new design process. Our former process, which we still use on occasion is called D4 (Drop Dead Design Day). It stems from a design process that had a hard stop day (the drop dead day), where no matter what, we had a design on paper and committed to it. Needless to say, it would consistently deliver well built robots, but it would be a bit of a compromise.

This year we are going to blow up the process and try something new. Some of the changes are listed below:

In order to participate in the D5, you must pass a test of the FTC rules. You will be tested on the following:

  1. Game Manual Part I

  2. Game Manual Part 2 Will only be available after 11am Central on 9/6/2014

  3. Drivetrain Design - featuring the Kitbot on Steroids by Ben Bennet

While you will not be explicitly tested on the following, these are very good to read and understand:

  1. FTC Sensor Guide

  2. FTC Robot Wiring Guide

  3. Samantha Module User Guide

Currently the test is scheduled for Tuesday 9/9 after school in Bertucciland. There will be one makeup for those that cannot make the exam and are pre-excused. Emphasis on the pre-excused. This means communication from you to me why you will not make it well prior to the exam. There will be a makeup exam on Thursday 9/11 after school in Bertucciland for those that miss the original exam and those that fail the first one. There will be no more tests this round. If you don’t pass either of these two exams you don’t participate in the design meetings. Period.

Daniel Teal

@dteal
9/4/2014 19:49

Great FTC Information: see the wiring guide, Samantha guide, and FTC sensor guide at http://www.usfirst.org/roboticsprograms/ftc/team-resources.

Gerry Cocco

@gerrycocco
9/4/2014 19:56

I’ll link them above later…they look good

FTC R1D2 Done - what about R2D2?

Update 9/15/2014 Feedback meeting this week scheduled on 9/16 (Tues) or 9/18 (Thurs) for each group who presented. Coordinate schedule with Gerry.

Update 9/9/2014

Some other team members: Becky, Travis, Jackson, Henry, Sum Kidd, Jonathan, Kelly, Kyla, Hunter, Harper and Blake wanted to try their hand at design. Given that the design process for D5 should only have about 6 members on the design team, all members should be fully versed in the rules and strategy, and there are not effective time limits on the discussion…. we in effect did an old style D4. Warts and all. R2D2 was done with a D4 process. After much contentious discussion, the team divided up into 3 design teams (need to note those groups and group leaders here…), and will go off and design separately.

We will be meeting again on Thursday 9/11 to review designs. Members of R1D2 and myself will evaluate the designs for taking some of them on to the prototype stage. Not all designs (if any) will make it. The design team can choose to make the prototype or farm it out to the R1D2 team. If we choose to make a prototype, we want a well constructed proof of concept.

Update 9/7/2014

The prototype is done. We have two manipulator designs that “work”, but need a lot of refinement. Proof of concept = excellent. Pretty…not so much. Lots of duct tape and zip ties…some imagination is also required. We will be showing it off to the public SOON. Why not now you ask? Well here is the reason.

Six email “challenged” or otherwise non-observant people “missed” the notes that we were going to try R1D2. Six people read the mail and responded and took part. The six that took part had an excellent time, as did I. Since we are still fine tuning this D5 process which R1D2 is only a test phase, we decided we could run another R2D2 (Robot 2 in 2 Days) with one more group of six (6). That will be the FIRST SIX that respond to the email that I’m going to send out shortly. Emphasis on respond.

We have explicitly tried to keep the final R1D2 designs under wraps to have the “second set of eyes” be untainted. This is both to find new ideas, and potentially reinforce what we found. So if you wanted to be on R1D2, here is your chance to be on R2D2. The note will go out soon. This is a time sensitive and time limited offer.

After the R2D2 meets (if enough want to), we will unveil the R1D2 prototype in the shop as it it tweaked and improved.

Update 9/6/2014

We attended the Vandegrift Kickoff. Took part in and won the first Balloon Tower team building exercise! We did well on many others as well. In fact lots of folks did well. I would say feedback on the team building was all positive. It was definitely worth doing and worth coming back next year.

We had the game reveal which was interesting and everyone got right down to the rules and kicking around ideas. One negative on this is that they didn’t do any mixing of teams for cross pollination of ideas. Some of our team wanted to see what other teams did for design, but that didn’t happen.

Another minor disappointment is that the Sacone’s Pizza was for Vandegrift only. We got Gatti’s (or something like that). Well if you are from NY and had Sacone’s before you could understand why this New Yorker was annoyed we didn’t get Sacone’s pizza…but then our pizza was FREE, so I can’t really complain.

We cut out of the Kickoff at 1pm when the emphasis moved to what the Rookie teams should know and/or do. We went back to the Spurflower B&B (my house) and started the R1D2 prototype process. Today we covered rules, strategy and the manipulator design space. We believe that the FOD mecanum drive developed over the summer will be great for this game.

We took a break for home cooked pasta dinner and then went out shopping for some plastic balls (baseball size and golfball size) like in the game. We got those at Academy and we went to Home Depot to buy some pipes! More on that on Monday.

We ended around 8 or so and got everyone back home for a good nights sleep. Tomorrow we will start build of our top idea and see where things go. Wish us luck.

Update 9/4/2014:

Thursday/Friday

  • we load up Marek’s car with all the things on our “list” of parts and pieces, robots, etc that we need to build over the weekend. Marek will bring it home and have it ready for us when we arrive on Sunday at 9am.

Saturday

  • we will meet at Vandegrift at 9am; Attend the team building, unveil, lunch and strategy session. We will leave a 1pm and head to Gerry’s

I’ll start the home made spaghetti sauce so the house smells good for the entire design time. Hungry designers are good designers :-). We will go until about 8pm +/- depending on how things go. I suspect 8pm should be fine. Then everyone goes home as they got here and gets a good nights sleep and can do some homework.

Sunday

Gerry to pickup Miles and Izzy
